Thought for 73s Creating a Custom Cockpit Extension for NVIDIA GPU Metrics To create a custom Cockpit extension that displays NVIDIA GPU metrics (e.g., utilization, temperature) fetched from Performance Co-Pilot (PCP) via the NVIDIA PMDA, follow these steps. This involves using the Cockpit Starter Kit for a React-based page, integrating PCP data retrieval, and packaging for installation. The extension will appear as a new menu item in Cockpit, showing GPU stats in a widget-like format without requiring a full separate dashboard. 1. Setup Development Environment Install prerequisites: Node.js (for npm), git, and Cockpit packages on Ubuntu 24.04 (e.g., sudo apt install cockpit npm git). Clone the Starter Kit repository: text git clone https://github.com/cockpit-project/starter-kit.git cd starter-kit Install dependencies and build: text npm install make Symlink for local testing: text mkdir -p ~/.local/share/cockpit ln -s $(pwd)/dist ~/.local/share/cockpit/gpu-monitor This creates a base "Starter Kit" page accessible at https://localhost:9090/starter-kit; rename to "gpu-monitor" in subsequent steps. 2. Configure manifest.json Edit manifest.json in the project root to define the extension: json { "version": 1, "requires": { "cockpit": "200" }, "tools": { "gpu-monitor": { "label": "GPU Monitor", "path": "index.html", "keywords": [ { "matches": ["gpu", "nvidia", "metrics"] } ] } }, "content-security-policy": "default-src 'self' 'unsafe-inline'; form-action 'self'; connect-src 'self' ws: wss:" } The tools section adds a "GPU Monitor" item under "Tools" in Cockpit's menu. Adjust requires for Cockpit version compatibility. 3. Implement the JavaScript Code for GPU Metrics Edit src/index.jsx (React component) to fetch and display PCP NVIDIA metrics. Use Cockpit's API (cockpit.spawn) to run PCP commands like pmrep for real-time GPU data (assuming NVIDIA PMDA is installed and active). Example code structure: jsx import cockpit from 'cockpit'; import React, { useState, useEffect } from 'react'; import { Card, CardTitle, CardBody, Grid, GridItem } from '@patternfly/react-core'; const GPUMonitor = () => { const [metrics, setMetrics] = useState({ utilization: 'N/A', temperature: 'N/A' }); useEffect(() => { const interval = setInterval(() => { cockpit.spawn(["pmrep", "-s", "1", "-t", "1s", "nvidia.gpu.utilization", "nvidia.gpu.temperature"]) .then(output => { const lines = output.split('\n'); const data = lines[lines.length - 2].split(/\s+/); // Parse last metric line setMetrics({ utilization: data[1] || 'N/A', temperature: data[2] || 'N/A' }); }) .catch(error => console.error('Error fetching metrics:', error)); }, 5000); // Poll every 5 seconds return () => clearInterval(interval); }, []); return ( GPU Utilization {metrics.utilization}% GPU Temperature {metrics.temperature}°C ); }; document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", () => { ReactDOM.render(, document.getElementById('app')); }); This uses PatternFly for widget styling, polls PCP metrics, and updates the UI. Extend for more metrics (e.g., nvidia.gpu.memory.used). Handle errors and multiple GPUs by parsing pmrep output. 4. Update HTML and CSS In po.js, ensure translations if needed (optional for English-only). Edit index.html template in src/: html GPU Monitor
Build with make to compile JSX to JS and bundle. 5. Test the Extension Run make to rebuild. Access Cockpit at https://localhost:9090, log in, and navigate to "Tools" > "GPU Monitor". Verify metrics display; use browser console for debugging. Run tests: make check (requires Vagrant for VM testing). 6. Package and Install Build RPM for distribution: make rpm. For manual install, copy dist/ to /usr/share/cockpit/gpu-monitor/ (system-wide) or symlink to ~/.local/share/cockpit/. Verify with cockpit-bridge --packages. Restart Cockpit socket if needed: systemctl restart cockpit.socket. This creates a lightweight, integrated GPU widget. Ensure PCP NVIDIA PMDA is active (pmcd running) for metrics. For advanced features like real-time graphs, integrate Chart.js via npm and update the React component. 8 web pages 3.1s Is this going to be possible? EOF # Edit src/index.jsx cat > src/index.jsx << EOF import cockpit from 'cockpit'; import React, { useState, useEffect } from 'react'; import { Card, CardTitle, CardBody, Grid, GridItem } from '@patternfly/react-core'; const GPUMonitor = () => { const [metrics, setMetrics] = useState({ utilization: 'N/A', temperature: 'N/A' }); useEffect(() => { const interval = setInterval(() => { cockpit.spawn(["pmrep", "-s", "1", "-t", "1s", "nvidia.gpu.utilization", "nvidia.gpu.temperature"]) .then(output => { const lines = output.split('\n'); const data = lines[lines.length - 2].split(/\s+/); setMetrics({ utilization: data[1] || 'N/A', temperature: data[2] || 'N/A' }); }) .catch(error => console.error('Error fetching metrics:', error)); }, 5000); return () => clearInterval(interval); }, []); return ( GPU Utilization {metrics.utilization}% GPU Temperature {metrics.temperature}°C ); }; document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", () => { ReactDOM.render(, document.getElementById('app')); }); EOF # Build npm install make # Install extension system-wide mkdir -p /usr/share/cockpit/gpu-monitor cp -r dist/* /usr/share/cockpit/gpu-monitor/ # Clean up cd / rm -rf /tmp/gpu-monitor # Restart Cockpit systemctl restart cockpit.socket bash #!/bin/bash # Reversal script set -e # Stop and disable services systemctl stop cockpit.socket pmlogger pmcd systemctl disable cockpit.socket pmlogger pmcd # Uninstall NVIDIA PMDA if [ -d /var/lib/pcp/pmdas/nvidia ]; then cd /var/lib/pcp/pmdas/nvidia && ./Remove fi # Purge packages apt purge -y cockpit cockpit-pcp pcp gettext nodejs npm make git apt autoremove -y # Remove extension rm -rf /usr/share/cockpit/gpu-monitor # Clean up any residuals rm -rf /tmp/gpu-monitor 20 web pages 2.9s md@nn06:~$ nano cp.sh && chmod +x cp.sh && ./cp.sh ==== AUTHENTICATING FOR org.freedesktop.systemd1.manage-units ==== Authentication is required to stop 'cockpit.socket'.
